Hunting Ends in Death: Gun Explodes in the Barrel, Zhao Guanda Dies Instantly 177

Zhao Guanda, a villager in Gaoqiao, Pudong, was fond of hunting. Every day, he carried a gun to the fields to hunt. The day before yesterday, he went to the fields about ten miles away from the town. He spotted a giant bird flying in the sky, raised his gun, and aimed to fire. Unexpectedly, the gun exploded in the barrel, and the bullet flew backward, hitting Zhao's head and other parts, causing him to fall to the ground and die instantly. Villagers saw this and inquired in the town. Zhao's family then went to investigate and wanted to collect the body. However, the Third District Fourth Police Station, considering that the matter involved human life, ordered the local security officer Gao Linquan to report it to the local court for examination. Zhao's family petitioned the court for exemption from the examination.

Medical Student Yao Wenrang Commits Suicide, Checked into the Hongkou Hotel, Critically Ill after Taking Poison 178

Yao Wenrang, a Cantonese man, 22 years old, wearing a suit and leather shoes, was an elegant young man. He rented a room at No. 17 Daderi, North Sichuan Road, and was studying at the China Medical College on Bazhi Road. At around nine o'clock the night before, he suddenly checked into the Hongkou Hotel on North Sichuan Road with his friend. He was guided to Room 43 on the second floor. Because the room was small, with only one single bed, the two of them shared a bed, which was uncomfortable. At around twelve o'clock, Yao checked into Room 54 to sleep. When entering the hotel, he wrote on the registration book that he was a Cantonese man named Guang Youtian from the academic community, and his friend's name was Tuo Lei. Then they separated and went to sleep. Until eleven o'clock yesterday morning, his friend got up and went to Room 54. He knocked on the door several times, but there was no answer for a long time. Suspecting something was wrong, he called the tea boy, who pried open the glass window and entered the room. He saw that Yao's face had turned pale and he was delirious. It was suspected that he had taken poison. He immediately reported to the police station by telephone and ordered an ambulance to the scene, which rushed him to Tongren Hospital for treatment. His life was in critical condition.

Wang Yunqu is Granted a Divorce from Wang Mulu, One-Sided Debate Ends in Judgment 179

Wang Mulu, the son of Suzhou silk merchant Wang Xingyi, studied medicine and married Ms. Wang Yunqu. In the early days of their marriage, they were quite harmonious and had several children. Years ago, Mulu's business in the south was sluggish, and the business run by his father also declined. He went north to Tianjin and Jinzhou to seek a living. After becoming a traveler, he indulged in debauchery and became addicted to opium. Ms. Wang feared that her husband would become addicted to pleasure and degenerate over time. She once went to Tianjin, hoping to persuade him to return. However, Mulu suddenly forgot their old affection and avoided seeing her. She had to return south in resentment, and her father-in-law, Xingyi, no longer continued to support her. So she hired lawyer Chen Tingrui to sue Xingyi in the First Special District Local Court, requesting funds to maintain her livelihood. The court summoned both father-in-law and daughter-in-law and persuaded them to reconcile. Wang Xingyi agreed to pay Wang Yunqu and her five children 20 yuan a month and to be responsible for the education, clothing, and food expenses. The case was settled with signatures in court. Unexpectedly, Wang Xingyi was unwilling to part with a single hair and would rather break his promise to his daughter-in-law and grandchildren than provide funds for their support. His son, Mulu, was recently convicted by the local court in Tianjin for privately smoking opium and imprisoned in the Hebei Third Prison. Xingyi loved his son deeply and paid money for him, which made Wang Yunqu feel that the Wang family treated them differently and that they were extremely ungrateful. In order to seek a thorough solution, she hired lawyer Chen again to file a divorce lawsuit against Mulu and requested that the defendant be ordered to pay living expenses and return the dowry. The First Special Court held several hearings. The defendant knew he was in the wrong and avoided appearing. Judge Peng allowed the one-sided debate to end and pronounced judgment yesterday, granting the plaintiff Wang Yunqu a divorce from the defendant Wang Mulu, ordering the defendant to pay the plaintiff 5,000 yuan for alimony, and ordering that all the dowry should be returned to the plaintiff. The 1,300 yuan owed to the plaintiff should also be repaid, and the litigation costs should be borne by the defendant.

Improvement of the Beijing-Shanghai Line, Allocation Method of Passenger and Freight Cars, Reducing Waste and Developing Freight Transport 180

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration has recently prepared charts showing the density of monthly passenger numbers at various stations along the two lines and submitted them to the Ministry of Railways for verification. The Ministry of Railways believes that the number of seats provided on the current passenger trains on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway exceeds the demand and that the engine power used for passenger trains should be saved to develop freight transport. The Ministry of Railways also issued several instructions. The administration has followed these instructions. The details are recorded below:

Reducing Waste 181

The Ministry ordered a reduction in the number of through passenger trains running by three or four to avoid wasting passenger seats on the Nanjing-Changzhou section. The Ministry also suggested replacing the reduced number of through passenger trains with through mixed trains to balance passenger convenience with the development of freight transport. The administration complied and converted the 11th and 12th Beijing-Shanghai up and down third- and fourth-class trains into through mixed trains between Beijing and Shanghai. When departing from the departure station, the number of through passenger and freight cars attached was determined based on passenger and freight transport conditions and the engine's towing capacity, to fully consider passenger and freight transport needs.

Full Equipment 182

The Ministry ordered that Wuxi be used as a center and that sufficient car allocation equipment be added to the station so that when trains arrive at the station, they can be re-allocated according to passenger and freight transport needs before departing. The Changzhou, Suzhou, and Kunshan stations should also gradually add car allocation equipment. For the time being, the Wuxi station should be used as a freight transshipment center. All downbound mixed passenger and freight cars arriving at the station should have some freight cars detached and replaced with various types of passenger cars suitable for transporting passengers from Wuxi to Shanghai. Upbound mixed trains can have various types of passenger cars attached between Shanghai and Wuxi to transport passengers from Shanghai to Wuxi. After arriving in Wuxi, the number of passengers decreases, so some passenger cars can be detached and replaced with an appropriate number of freight cars to reach Nanjing. The administration complied and, when the 7th and 8th Beijing-Shanghai up and down express trains and the 9th Beijing-Shanghai downbound express train arrived at the Wuxi station, the number of passenger and freight cars were detached and attached according to passenger and freight transport conditions and the engine's towing capacity. If all freight cars at the Wuxi station could not be allocated into a train, the department should follow the usual practice and open short-distance freight trains at any time for transshipment. A shunting engine must be added at the Wuxi station so that after each train arrives, the passenger and freight cars to be attached and detached can be quickly arranged to avoid delaying the train's travel time. The locomotive department has also complied.

Mixed Trains 183

The Ministry ordered that mixed trains should be composed of one third-class passenger car, one baggage and car guard car, and the rest freight cars. If there are many passengers, passenger cars can be added and freight cars reduced to balance passenger and freight transport needs. The administration has complied with the order and converted the 19th and 24th Shanghai-Changzhou short-distance trains, the 21st and 22nd Shanghai-Wuxi short-distance trains, and the 23rd and 24th Wuxi-Beijing short-distance trains into mixed passenger and freight trains since the implementation of the Third Timetable, attaching freight cars in addition to the passenger cars. Now, the administration is again complying with the order to reduce the number of passenger cars attached and attach as many freight cars as possible to these and other short-distance trains, according to passenger and freight transport conditions along the line and the engine's towing capacity.

Ministry Instructions 184

The Ministry also issued two instructions: 1. Open short-distance freight trains between Shanghai and Wuxi to transship the freight cars detached from the downbound mixed trains at Wuxi and the freight cars transported to Wuxi to be attached to the upbound mixed trains to reach Nanjing. 2. For regular freight trains with faster travel times, third- and fourth-class passenger cars can be attached to sections with high passenger traffic when necessary. Since this involves changes to fares, speed, and stopping times, the administration plans to conduct a thorough study and plan before complying with the order to revise the 301st and 302nd Shanghai-Pinglian Through Train Timetable in March next year and implement it all at once.

Lecture Notes from the Engineering Society, Chen Ticheng Lectures on Highway Construction, Zheng Hua Lectures on the Nanjing Ferry Project 188

The Shanghai branch of the Chinese Institute of Engineers held its December regular meeting at the Bankers' Association Club on the evening of the 18th of this month. More than 50 people attended. After the dinner, Chairman Xu Peihuang reported on the recent situation of the association. Then, Mr. Chen Ticheng, director of the Highway Department of the National Economic Council, was invited to lecture on highway construction. Mr. Chen said that there is an urgent need for highways in our country. Although cars and gasoline come from foreign countries, it is inevitable that profits will flow out. However, all parties are currently trying to manufacture vehicles and search for oil-producing areas, which is not impossible to reverse. The methods of raising funds for road construction that are feasible in Europe and America are not suitable for our country. The method adopted by Zhejiang Province is to allow merchants to operate long-distance buses, collecting a contribution fee on one hand and using this contribution fee as collateral for borrowing money on the other hand to build other roads. This cycle has been quite effective. The width of the highway surface, the quality of its building materials, and other engineering matters depend on the transportation conditions and the ability to raise funds. Next, Dr. Zheng Hua, chief of the Design Section of the Ministry of Railways, was invited to lecture on the Nanjing Xiaguan Pukou ferry project. Dr. Zheng briefly said that the Jinpu and Jinghu railways are separated by the Yangtze River, and there has long been a desire to connect them. Since the water is very deep, it is not suitable to build tunnels or bridges. A ferry should be used. However, the water level varies by two feet between winter and summer, so it is necessary to find a way to compensate. The British suggested using a ship with two decks. The Dutch suggested using a floating dock ferry. The Americans suggested using a rocking bed principle of construction. I studied bridge engineering and thought of using a movable approach bridge to solve the problem. The plan was completed and sent abroad for estimation. The price was relatively cheap, so it was implemented. The Pukou and Xiaguan bridges are exactly the same. The bridge is more than 600 feet long and divided into four spans. Close to the beach, one end uses a pivot to connect the other spans. Each end and the adjacent end are suspended from the bridge tower with large screws. As the water level rises and falls, electricity is used to keep the span connected to the ferry level. The maximum slope of the other spans is 2%. The benches are single-track, but the span near the beach has three tracks. The ferry is 370 feet long and has three tracks, each 300 feet long, capable of carrying 20 40-ton cars. Each crossing of the river takes about one and a half hours. It has now been completed and is operating smoothly. The daily income is about 8,000 yuan. The benefits to itself are great, and the Jinghu Railway also benefits greatly. In the past, the railway's passenger transport was greater than its freight transport. Now the opposite is true and the business is booming. Both Mr. Chen and Mr. Zheng based their lectures on their expertise, carefully planned according to the domestic situation, adapted to the needs, and took into account both engineering and economics. It is a celebration for the country to have such talents. After the lectures, members asked questions and discussed them, showing a strong interest, which was unprecedented at past branch meetings. The meeting adjourned at more than ten o'clock.

Rapist Sentenced to Three and a Half Years in Prison: Gong Shunbing Admits Guilt Without Reservation 193

Gong Shunbing, a native of Wuxi, is twenty years old. Tram Derails and Collides with Truck: Fishmonger Falls and Dies: Mu Axiang Loses His Life Innocently 194

Mu Axiang, a Ningbo native, residing at No. 17 Puhua Lane, Dongyouheng Road, Hongkou, was a fishmonger. He operated a stall at the Tongzhou Road wet market. Every morning, he hired a truck to go to Xiaodongmen to purchase goods. At 4 a.m. on the 15th of this month, Mu hired a truck (F-1347) from the Xin Lianhe Trucking Company at the Taoyuan Lane entrance of the Tilanqiao. The driver, Zhao Yunlong from Jiangbei, drove south to purchase fresh fish from the fish market outside Xiaodongmen and loaded it onto the truck. Mu also sat next to the goods on the way back north to sell them. Unexpectedly, at 6 a.m., the truck was traveling north along the Bund when, at the intersection of Avenue Edward VII, tram No. 47 of route 8 of the British Tramway Company, which ran between Yangshupu and the 16th Pier, was traveling south. When it reached the intersection of Avenue Edward VII, the pointsman mistakenly switched the tracks, causing the tram to mistakenly take the wrong route. The tram turned west into the intersection of Avenue Edward VII when the truck was also speeding north, causing the two vehicles to be unable to brake and stop, resulting in a collision. Mu, who was sitting on the truck, was shaken off and fell, suffering a head injury and bleeding profusely. Both vehicles were damaged. The police recorded the license plate numbers and sent the injured person and the vehicles to Renji Hospital and reported to the police station. However, Mu died at 10 p.m. the night before due to his severe injuries. The hospital notified the police station, which transported the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home for an autopsy. Yesterday, the French police vehicle affairs department reported to the Second Special District Court, which appointed Prosecutor Wang Ren to conduct an autopsy with the forensic doctor. The official sat in court, and Mu Shengmu, the father of the deceased, stated that the deceased was his son, who died tragically from a car accident and requested justice. The official questioned the truck driver Zhao Yunlong and the tram driver Shi Wanqian about the circumstances of the accident. The official announced that Mu Axiang had died from a head injury caused by a collision between the vehicles. The body was claimed by the father for burial. The vehicle affairs department will investigate the negligence of the defendants and handle the case according to law.

Fire Erupts in Taikoo Kitchen: Stove Fire Erupts, Mistaken for Fire: Two Cooks Injured: Nothing Burned 200

At 1:50 p.m. yesterday, a coal fire in the rice cooking stove in the kitchen on the second floor of the British Taikoo Steamship Company on Xinkaihe in the French Concession suddenly erupted. Smoke filled the room, and a neighbor who saw it thought it was a fire and broke the fire alarm glass. The fire alarm rang immediately, causing tension among all the staff. After a while, the French Concession Fire Brigade received the news and rushed to the scene with as many as eleven fire trucks. The road on Yong'an Street was crowded with firefighters. They were about to drag the hoses to put out the fire, but the smoke on the upper floor had already dissipated. After checking, nothing was burned. Only two cooks were burned on their faces, wrists, and feet. The injuries were minor and they were not sent to the hospital. The firefighters saw that there was no fire and investigated the area before withdrawing. According to Ma Fuqing from Jiangbei, one of the injured cooks, the cause of the accident was that he was cleaning the room after the meal and put the swept garbage into the stove to burn it. Unexpectedly, when he put the garbage in, there was a sudden loud bang, and smoke and fire shot out, causing him to be burned. Another cook from Suzhou was also affected, but fortunately, his injuries were minor, and neither of them went to the hospital. However, all the staff were scared.

Iron Bar Falls from Balcony: Hits Two Children, One Dead, One Injured: Public Works Department Does Not Allow Alteration: Liu Ma's Children Die Unjustly 201

Liu Ma, a woman from Shandong, who lives in a kitchen at No. 44 Tai'an Lane, Beishan West Road, has a son and a daughter. The son is named Mao Tou and the daughter is named Axiang, both of whom are very young. At noon on the 15th of this month, the two children were playing at the entrance when, unexpectedly, an iron bar about ten feet long fell from the balcony of the house and hit the children's heads and other parts, causing serious injuries. Their mother saw it and sent Mao Tou and others to Shanghai Sanitarium for treatment. Axiang was more seriously injured and died the day before yesterday despite all efforts. Mao Tou is still being treated in the hospital, and his life cannot be predicted. The hospital reported to the Huishi Police Station, which ordered detectives to investigate. It was learned that the iron bar, which was dropped by Yin Zhonghe, the second landlord of the house, was used to support the bamboo for drying clothes. It was very strong, but Yin planned to build another small house on the balcony, so he removed the iron bar. However, this was discovered by the Sanitary Department of the Public Works Department, which did not allow it due to regulations. Therefore, Yin had no choice but to call a mason to reinstall the original iron bar, but because it was not installed securely, it suddenly fell the day before yesterday. The detectives carried the girl's body to the Feilun Road Autopsy Center. Yesterday, Prosecutor Diao Chengtang, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan, clerk Wang Zuyi, and others, were appointed by the First Special District Court to conduct an autopsy. Liu Ma, the mother of the deceased, testified about the previous situation. Diao then announced that Liu Axiang, a female, had died from a head injury caused by the iron bar before her death. The body was given to her mother, Liu Ma, who signed a guarantee to take it back for burial.

Can New Signs Be Charged with Additional House Tax? Yuan Yuan Hat Shop Requests Arbitration: Taxpayer Association Forwards Letter to Public Works Department 203

The Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayer Association sent a letter to the Director-General of the Public Works Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "According to a letter from the Yuan Yuan Hat Shop, 'Our shop is located at the corner of Shandong Road and Jiujiang Road. The old Public Works Department street numbers were 213 to 216, and the new street numbers are now 320 and 324. The monthly rent is 434 yuan and 15 cents. The Public Works Department has always calculated the total tax at 14% of the rent, and the monthly total tax is 60 yuan and 2 cents, which is 180 yuan and 6 cents per quarter. Now, when the Public Works Department collected the winter tax, it changed the 180 yuan and 6 cents on the tax bill to 193 yuan and 2 cents in red ink, which means that the scattered rent is falsely increased by 30 yuan per month. Our shop believed that the Public Works Department should not increase the tax for no reason and consulted with the Westerners who collect the tax below. They instructed us to contact the Western leader of the house tax in room 263 on the third floor with the tax bill. A Chinese person named Yao translated in that room, saying that the 14% calculation of our shop's tax bill was correct, but because our shop had recently been renovated and used chrome-plated sign letters, etc., which were quite valuable, the monthly rent had to be increased by 30 yuan. Our manager stated that it was actually because the market was sluggish and business was poor, so the facade was renovated in order to attract customers. Our shop's building had an old-fashioned wooden balcony, which had been in disrepair for many years and was about to collapse. We were afraid that it would injure pedestrians, so we discussed with the landlord to remove the wooden balcony. But after the wooden balcony was removed, the appearance was not very beautiful, so we slightly embellished it with a cement false wall. All of this was done as a last resort. How can we increase the tax burden again? Unexpectedly, the Westerner said that the tax must be increased, at least about 20 yuan. We think that at a time when the market is declining and all industries are depressed, the Public Works Department should reduce taxes to ease the difficulties of businesses. It is reasonable not to impose heavy taxes on merchants because of their unavoidable difficulties and facade renovations, and then to take the opportunity to increase the size of the house and extort merchants. In terms of renovation, three or four out of ten shops on various roads have closed down due to the poor market. But if there are occasional new shops opening, they will definitely re-renovate. Should the Public Works Department not calculate the actual rent and increase the tax? For example, in the Nanjing Road area, the same house with the same rent often changes tenants several times a year. In that year, the house must be renovated several times. Does the Public Works Department want to increase the tax several times within a year? In terms of the value of the renovation, for example, there are several similar houses in the same concession, rented to people. Suppose there is a tenant who installs his own water heater, installs new electric heating and cooling equipment, and everything inside is decorated luxuriously. The walls are also painted and the windows are changed. The cost is very high. Does the Public Works Department also want to increase the tax according to the value of the decoration? This is truly an unreasonable argument. Therefore, Yao's statement that the tax should be increased because the chrome-plated sign letters are of great value is absurd. But the Westerner has been asking to see our shop's renovation accounts, and our shop is very disturbed. We hereby present the whole story and ask you to forward the details to the Public Works Department and ask the Chinese directors to arbitrate with the bureau to ease the difficulties of businesses. This would be greatly appreciated. The association believes that municipal taxes should be based on the actual rent, which is the most legal and reasonable method, and is respected by your bureau. Taxpayers are very admired. Now that this case has occurred, the reason for increasing the rent is the value of the sign. The association firmly believes that your bureau will not have such a random financial policy, or that lower-level employees are seeking something else through this. The red ink used to change the donation ticket is already suspicious. In short, municipal taxes should be based on the actual rent, and falsely increasing the rent is a tax increase, which is in fundamental conflict with the resolution of the Taxpayers' Meeting. If a lower-level employee is acting recklessly, it should be considered an overreach of authority. If it is a case of ulterior motives, it should be considered dereliction of duty. According to the letter, we hereby request your bureau to order your subordinates to collect the total tax based on the actual rent, and not to disturb and interfere with the law."

Labor Dispute at Yufeng Cotton Mill in Zhengzhou: Cotton Control Committee Sends Personnel to Investigate the Truth 204

Regarding the long-standing labor dispute at the Yufeng Cotton Mill in Zhengzhou, nearly 369 bales of yarn stored in the factory were carried away by the workers, who intended to sell the yarn to provide for their living expenses. It has been learned that the Cotton Control Committee has sent technical specialist Tong Lüqing to Zhengzhou to investigate the truth of the case on the ground. The letter from the Banking Association to the Cotton Control Committee and the reply from the Cotton Control Committee are recorded below.

Banking Association Letter 205

"Our association, on behalf of the China, Shanghai, and Zhejiang Industrial Banks, has seized the cotton yarn of the Yufeng Cotton Mill in Zhengzhou, which was forcibly taken by the factory's union, causing a dispute. We have telegraphed the authorities in Beijing and Henan, as well as your association, to uphold justice. Recently, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce sent a telegram stating, 'Having read the telegram, we learned that the labor dispute at the Yufeng Cotton Mill in Zhengzhou has been unresolved for a long time. According to the Henan Provincial Construction Department, the factory has violated the decision in the past and refused mediation in the future. The responsible personnel have avoided meeting. The chairman of the factory, Mu Xiangyue, telegraphed that the cotton mill has been mortgaged to Shenchang Foreign Company and that the company's resident representative, Mr. Stimpert, has taken over, etc. Mediation cannot be carried out. However, thousands of workers are desperate for life and are starving and freezing. Although they have received very good training, they may be incited by reactionaries. The future is very worrying, etc.' We have ordered the department to handle the matter fairly to avoid trouble. According to the previous situation in the telegram, in addition to re-ordering the department, we hereby reply by telegram, etc. From the perspective of the current telegram from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, the inside story is very complicated and cannot be mediated in a few words. The China and other three banks are in danger of losing their seized goods. For this reason, we ask your association whether it can select capable personnel to go directly to the site to investigate the truth and find ways to remedy the situation, so that the seized goods will not be sold without authorization. The matter is urgent, and we are looking forward to it.'"

Cotton Control Committee Reply 206

"Having received your letter of December 13, stating that the labor dispute at the Yufeng Cotton Mill has been unresolved for a long time and that the situation is complicated, and requesting that we send personnel to investigate the truth and find ways to remedy the situation, we have appointed technical specialist Tong Lüqing of our association to go to Zhengzhou in the near future to investigate the truth and assist in resolving the situation. We have also telegraphed the Ministry of Industry and Commerce in Nanjing, Chairman Liu in Kaifeng, the Henan Provincial Construction Department, the Zheng County Government, and the Zheng County Chamber of Commerce to assist Specialist Tong when he arrives in Henan. A copy of the above telegram is enclosed for your review. After Specialist Tong arrives in Zheng County and handles the matter together, we will report the progress to you."

Post Office Issues Airmail Envelopes 209

The Shanghai Postal Administration issued a notice yesterday stating that the post office has now produced special airmail envelopes for sending airmail letters, available in both Chinese and Western styles. These are stocked at the counters of various post offices. The Western-style envelope is 11 cm in height and 15 cm in width. The front is printed with two dark blue horizontal lines, with space left above the two horizontal lines for affixing stamps. Between the two lines, the words "Par Aviou" are printed. On the left side of the vertical lines, the words "Airmail" are printed. The Chinese-style envelope has wavy green lines printed around the four edges of the front and back covers. In the center of the front, a rectangular box is printed in red for writing the recipient's name. In the upper left corner, the word "Airmail" is also printed, making it very conspicuous. The public is welcome to imitate the design if they wish. If airmail letters are sent using ordinary envelopes, blue airmail labels must still be affixed. These labels can be obtained directly from the post offices. Otherwise, if the above regulations are not followed, and the item is not sent by airmail, the post office will not be responsible.

According to his reply, the existing detention center of the Shanghai Local Court was only a two-story building, accommodating more than 200 prisoners. However, by this summer, the number had reached more than 800. The building was insufficient, so approval was obtained from superiors to allocate 50,000 yuan to rebuild a new three-story detention center on the original site. After three months of construction, it was completed at the beginning of last month. The center can accommodate more than 1,000 prisoners. In addition, the Shanghai Local Court originally had twelve courtrooms, which have now been increased to fourteen. Further additions will be made as needed based on the actual situation.

Fire on Zhoujiazui Road; Losses Estimated at Over 2,000 Yuan 212

Feng Shunji Carpentry Shop, located at No. 101, Lane, Zhoujiazui Road, Yangshupu, caught fire carelessly at 10:22 last night. Immediately, smoke filled the air and flames shot up. After the fire brigade rushed to the scene, they made every effort to extinguish the fire, which was finally put out at 11:00. Four bungalows of the shop were burned down, along with a large quantity of lumber. Losses are estimated at over 2,000 yuan.

The Tobacco and Exchange Industries to Discuss License Tax Today 216

Since the autumn of this year, the collection of tobacco and liquor license tax for Shanghai Bao has been undertaken by Ding Jinsheng, chairman of the Shanghai Shaoxing Wine Industry Association, as the chief collector. Because the contracted amount is too large, the collection and remittance are reportedly very different. It is said that there is a large difference. Now, under the order of the sub-bureau director, rectification will be carried out, and it is stipulated that starting from January 1st of next year, it must be strictly implemented and collected according to regulations. Letters have been sent to the two associations of Shanghai Bao to comply. It is heard that the Tobacco and Exchange Industry Association will convene a meeting of members today to decide on a method. First, they will negotiate with the tax authorities, requesting that they continue to collect taxes as usual in order to show consideration and avoid misunderstandings. The reason is that most of the businesses in this industry are small shops, operating with meager capital and earning only a small profit to support their families, which is truly difficult. They have been donating two yuan per quarter for the license. If rectified according to the regulations of the Ministry, they will have to pay four yuan per quarter. Other larger stores will generally increase their tax level according to their business situation and in accordance with regulations, fearing that it will be difficult to bear if implemented. A remedy is planned, and the tax authorities are scheduled to meet this Monday to discuss the matter. However, they have not yet met. Therefore, a notice was issued to the North and South Shanghai offices yesterday, calling for an emergency meeting to be convened nearby to determine a policy. The two offices immediately forwarded the notice to all representatives to discuss the matter at a meeting at 3:00 p.m. today. The meeting in Nanshi will be held at No. 427 Fumin Road, and the meeting in Beishi will be held at No. 8 Wanxiang Lane, Ai'erjin Road, on the same day.

City Voice 218

Special Sacrifice in Winter Low Prices: Every year when winter arrives, merchants in this city hold big sales. Among these big sales, there are even more special sacrifices. For example, the Samsung Cotton and Iron Factory on Nanjing Road and Shilu West Road is holding a winter sale because customers have loved its products for a year. Not only are various cotton fabrics sold at 30% or 20% off the original price, but even items sacrificed at half price are prepared. These half-price items are the factory's most famous colorfast electric cloth, as well as various colored serges and checkered thick flannels, all of which are daily necessities for families.

Excellent Products from Zhenxing Woolen Mill: The Shuanglong brand four-strand and six-strand woolen yarn produced by the Zhenxing Woolen Textile Mill on Xujiahui Road in this city is a giant among domestic woolen yarns. Since its launch, it has spread throughout the country. With the arrival of winter, sales are even stronger. Anyone who sells this woolen yarn enjoys generous profits, so major domestic product companies both inside and outside the city are happy to promote it. The factory also has a kind of Xuechi soft flannel, which has an elastic body and is completely comparable to Vienna from a certain country, but the price is less than one-third. After investigation by reporters, it was learned that the raw materials for this product are top-quality wool, mixed with a small amount of kapok, and spun and refined using the latest technology. It is very suitable for clothing in all seasons, regardless of men, women, old or young. It is heard that the factory's store in the Penglai Market, in addition to selling various self-made clothing fabrics and Shuanglong brand woolen yarn, also sells other items such as bathrobes, towels, bed sheets, and various colored shirt fabrics to meet customer needs.

Mingyuan Ji Hotel Opens: Mingyuan Ji Hotel is located in Helefang, Fourth Malu, in a convenient location. All the rooms have been newly painted, and the room rates are low, with many rooms around five corners, which are in line with the people's economization. The comfort of the beds and the cleanliness of the bedding are especially important. The tea servants are attentive, and the wine costs are not counted. According to the hotel, there are many unique features. From the beginning of its establishment, it has been thinking of the travelers, which is incomparable to other hotels. Anyone who wants physical and mental comfort should try it.

Shanghai Silk Industry Bank Gives Away Exquisite Calendars: Shanghai Silk Industry Bank, located at No. 64 Hankou Road in this city, has been making rapid progress in business recently, and its future is quite promising. In order to reward customers, more than 10,000 exquisite calendars have been specially made. All new and old savings account holders who open fixed-term accounts at the head office and branches will receive them as gifts upon presentation of their certificates.

The Second Issue of the Second Volume of the Far East Monthly is Published: The second issue of the second volume of the Far East Monthly has now been published. The content is rich, the opinions are accurate, and the texts in this issue are particularly important. In terms of treatises, there are Zhang Jun-guang's "World War II and China", Fan Jue-tao's "Increased Unemployment and Population War in Italy", Lan Lin's "Does Zhang Dongsun Understand Dialectics?", Shen Ruo-bing's "The Origins of the Third Kind of People" and Ye Qian-chu's "The Recent Economic Situation in China", all of which are insightful and unique. In addition to Ms. Du's long novel, there is also Tu Yangci's "Xia Ferry", a short story depicting the military warlords' poisoning of rural areas, and Huang Zhenxia's "Elegy of Northern Manchuria", a military novel predicting the Russo-Japanese War. The subscription office is located at No. 221 Saposai Road, Shanghai.

1934 Radio Telegraph Operator's Must-Know: Because the Radio Telegraph Operators of the China Radio Engineering School, No. 1395 Aidoo Road in this city, will follow the new Radio Convention Regulations and Practical Communications from 1934 onwards, the teacher Fan Fengyuan translated the new convention in English and French, selecting the key points. For example, the new allocation of international call signs, the new regulations on wavelength rates, distress calls such as SOS, XXX, PAN, MAYDAY, and the method of taking safety calls TTT, a list of abbreviations, etc., and also added the regulations and prices of the new code compiled by the Ministry of Communications to calculate the number of words. It also added the call signs of long and short wave radio stations across the country, the international radio stations of various countries in the world, the call signs of Chinese naval radio stations, the call signs of private radio stations in various provinces, the call signs of ship radio stations across the country, the signal methods of Chinese direction-finding radio stations such as Dajishan, Huadian Mountain and Sheshan, a list of times for weather reports from Chinese observatories and coastal radio stations, aviation abbreviations, photography telegraph abbreviations, an English-Chinese comparison of Chinese place names, the application and repair methods of all machinery in radio stations, and various communication methods and Q&A formats for telegraph operators. It is a huge book and a must-have for radio personnel. This book is currently being printed and will be published within ten days. Anyone who wants to ask for it should make a reservation with the school in advance. The price is one yuan and six corners per copy, with postage of seven points. There are not many copies left after the book is published, and it is feared that only 1,000 copies will be printed and will not be sold by bookstores. Outlying areas

Dai Yingguan Inspects Educational Conditions in Ji and Ping; No National Army East of Lutai; Thriving Japanese Language Research Support Associations 223

Dai Yingguan, Section Chief of the Ministry of Education, has returned from inspecting education in Hebei Province and Beiping City. The following is a description of his inspection of the educational conditions in Ji and Ping:

The most peculiar situation in Hebei Province's education sector is probably in the schools along the Beining Railway line. Since the signing of the so-called Tanggu Truce, the war zone has been nominally "taken over," and schools in various locations have勉强 (barely managed to) open. Besides the fact that school buildings have been damaged in many cases due to the stationing of Japanese and puppet troops, and that books, instruments, specimens, etc., have also been mostly damaged or lost, making immediate restoration impossible, all teaching and moral education in the schools are subjected to external pressure and cannot be carried out as usual. For example, the "Principles of the Party" subject is not allowed to be offered; the portrait and will of the late Premier Sun Yat-sen are not allowed to be displayed; memorial weeks are not allowed to be held. Even when lecturing on history, lecturers cannot speak freely regarding the tragic events and national humiliation facts of past years. Furthermore, the Japanese troops stationed in the area often send people to inspect the schools at will, and promote the establishment of Japanese language courses, introducing Japanese language teachers. In the Luan Dong area, Japanese Language Research Support Associations are established everywhere, enticing people to join and pay a membership fee of at least half a yuan per month to study Japanese. Calling them "Support Associations" clearly indicates that their purpose is more than just research. They tell the public that those who join the association can not only study Japanese but also receive protection. In other words, all members are guaranteed not to be anti-Japanese elements. Before each Support Association is established, it issues leaflets listing the titles and names of local political, academic, and business leaders as "supporters" for publicity. Those listed who dare to deny it are immediately labeled as anti-Japanese elements, and being anti-Japanese is tantamount to being reactionary, which can lead to immediate arrest. Therefore, those who have been designated as supporters do not dare to openly deny it, and the influence of the Support Associations grows daily. Now, branch associations have also been established in places like Tangshan in Luanxi, and it is likely that they will spread along the Beining line. An even more shocking matter is that there is a small mountain in Tangshan town where Chinese and Japanese people live together. Gambling dens, brothels, and opium dens have been opened, and kidnapping and extortion are rampant, with no evil left undone. The local Public Security Bureau once sent police to arrest more than 70 establishments, but they were interfered with by external forces and were forced to compensate the Japanese merchants for several thousand yuan in losses, and all those arrested were released. Afterwards, the merchants' influence became even greater, and the Public Security Bureau had to arrest more than 80 establishments a second time. The result was even more outrageous, with the release still occurring, and the compensation being increased. From then on, the merchants boldly wrote the words "Officially Approved Business" in front of their doors, and no one dared to question it. This kind of phenomenon is not only related to educational issues, but also makes social education absolutely impossible. The war zone is nominally a "non-armed zone," but the soldiers seen at each station along the Beining line are indeed numerous, especially east of Lutai, where our army is not allowed to go. The locals say, "No National Army east of Lutai," which is in stark contrast to the Japanese-backed Support Associations, which are constantly advancing westward. Apart from the Beining line, the overall educational situation in Hebei Province is still good. Taking secondary schools as an example, Tianjin has the renowned Nankai Middle School, Baoding has the long-established and talent-filled Yude Middle School, and there is also the rising Tongren Middle School, all of which can be considered excellent. The Tianjin Women's Teachers College, originally expanded from a women's normal school, still has normal and secondary school departments. Its science equipment and teaching conditions are probably rare among women's normal schools in various provinces. After the tragic incident last year at Baoding Normal School, Principal Xiao Hansan took over and thoroughly reformed it, purchasing more than 800 mu of land, divided into experimental and economic zones. Every afternoon, two classes of students work in the two zones, with each class spending three afternoons a week working entirely in the fields. The principal and teachers personally lead the way, and both zones have been inspected. The students work very hard and are extremely interested. The vocational schools in Baoding have three departments: textile, machinery, and applied chemistry. The textile chemistry department has female student classes that are well-developed. The practical training time does not differ much from the standards set by the ministry, and they can still be realistic. The secondary vocational department of Tianjin Institute of Technology can hardly utilize the factory equipment of the institute, and the students are not very developed. In general, the secondary education situation in places along the Pinghan Line, such as Baoding, Zhengding, Dingxian, and Cangzhou along the Jinpu Line, seems to be better than in Tianjin, especially in Baoding. There are ten public and private secondary schools in the area. Except for two schools that are small in scale, the rest have both spirit and form, and the students are very simple, disciplined, and fond of sports. The girls dress plainly, and the dormitories are extraordinarily simple and beautiful, forming a fashion. The teachers are all full-time and live with the students. The teachers in schools such as Tongren Zhicun have very low salaries, but they are full of spirit, leading the youth, and have a concept of regarding education as a sacred lifelong career, which is absolutely different from those in cities who calculate hours and salaries. The report of the League of Nations education observation group observes and criticizes our country's education with seriousness, which is not easy to fully understand without personally inspecting the local education situation. However, there is one point in the report, that is, the evaluation of the work of the Pingjiao Association in Dingxian, which seems to be inevitably biased. Because of the urgency of personal time, I did not have time to fully inspect the four major educations it advocates. However, in terms of women's art education and health education, its work is obviously not a waste, and the results are quite impressive. I once inspected the Pingmin Girls' School in Zong Sijun, only for a weekly meeting. The students' speeches and discussions, the use of words and expressions, are indeed quite trained, so it must not be judged by its appearance as a village girl and rejected from the door of modern education.

Tianjin used to be a municipality directly under the central government, but now it is an ordinary city. The education expenditure is 60,000 yuan per month, and no less than half of the children are out of school. There is one municipal normal school, but there are already one provincial male and one female normal school in the city. The city also sends two students to study in Europe and the United States, which is particularly inconsistent with the principle of financial economy. The allocation of secondary education funds in Hebei Province is too much for normal schools and too little for vocational schools. Normal schools used to be six years, but now they have been changed to three years. Many schools want to set up junior high schools to avoid budget cuts. Now, Director Chen has decided to allocate funds in accordance with the standards set by the ministry, and I sincerely hope that the responsible officials in the department will plan together and not have any fear of difficulty. All school principals should uphold the central government's intentions and not be afraid of making a new start, and progress can be expected. The local education funds in various counties of Hebei Province are not well-organized. The county heads in the interior counties are particularly irresponsible. When asked about the amount of education fees, most of them cannot answer. Moreover, almost every county has more than one rural normal school, and its expenditure rate is less than 5,000 yuan. The rural teachers feel struggling, while the county magistrate feels that it is not easy to develop primary school education. In the future, the establishment of rural teachers should be determined according to the local needs of teachers, and it is not necessary for every county to have a school, just to decorate the facade. (To be continued in Hebei Province and Beiping)

Zhou Bangdao, an inspector of the Ministry of Education, has completed his two-month inspection of education in Shaanxi and Henan provinces and returned to the ministry on the 18th to work. This Municipality's Elementary Schools Actively Prepare for Elementary School Students' Mandarin Speech Contest; To Be Held at 1:00 PM on the 31st of This Month at the Municipal Shuji Elementary School 226

At their last meeting, the principals of the elementary schools in this city decided to launch an elementary school Mandarin speech contest in order to develop public speaking skills and promote Mandarin habits. It has been decided that the contest will be held at the Municipal Shuji Elementary School starting at 1:00 PM on the 31st of this month. The preparations are described below:

Yesterday's Preparatory Meeting: The second preparatory meeting was held at Yizhao Elementary School at 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon. Weng Guoxun, He Yizhao, Zhang Junfei, and Wu Zhi attended. He Yizhao chaired the meeting, and Wu Zhi recorded the minutes. The following resolutions were passed: 1. Regarding the location: It was decided that the Municipal Shuji Elementary School would be the location. 2. Regarding how to issue notices: It was decided that the secretariat would handle it. 3. Regarding the registration location: It was decided that it would be at Minfu Elementary School. 4. Regarding inviting judges and soliciting prizes: It was decided that the secretariat would handle it. 5. Regarding how to keep and distribute the prizes: It was decided that the prizes would be kept by Yizhao Elementary School, and the distribution of prizes would be handled jointly by the preparatory members the day before the competition. 6. Regarding the date of the third preparatory meeting: It was decided that it would be at Binhai Elementary School at 9:00 AM on the 24th of this month. 7. Regarding how to specify the commemorative certificates: It was decided that He Yizhao would handle it. The meeting adjourned.

Regarding the Repossession of the Baseball Field, the Final Decision Still Awaits New York; The Expected Time is Around April Next Year 242

The Shanghai Times reported that there have been rumors recently that the Chinese Baseball Field, which is currently leased by the National Sports Association, will soon be converted into a school. Yesterday, the reporter learned from a reliable source that the association can continue to lease it until next spring, as the site is the property of the Rockefeller Foundation, which has been purchasing it since 1914, and the original cost has reached 298,000 US dollars, and the market price is even higher. It is currently being used as a sports field by the Sports Association with a small rent. Recently, discussions have been held on the use of the land in order to achieve the original purpose of the purchase, but according to reliable sources, the final decision still awaits New York, and the expected time is around April next year. The original purpose of the Rockefeller Foundation's purchase of the land was to establish a medical school. In the future, it will probably be relocated here by the National Medical College. The school was originally in Wusong, but it was destroyed in the Shanghai War of 1928. It is currently temporarily housed in the Red Cross Hospital.

West Qing Basketball: Pirates Defeat Zhizhi Again; St. John's Loses to Jiangwan 247

Last night, only two Group A matches took place in the West Qing Basketball League. The Pirates defeated Zhizhi in a one-sided game, with a final score of 83-36. Jiangwan defeated St. John's in a closely contested match, 41-32.

Pirates Defeat Zhizhi: Initially, the Pirates were not in good form, and their lines were disorganized. Consequently, they were at a disadvantage when facing Zhizhi. However, Zhizhi's poor shooting accuracy, with only two successful shots out of nine attempts, allowed the Pirates to gain an advantage after six minutes, thanks to Smith's short throws. From then on, the Pirates' prowess gradually emerged, and their forwards remained calm and composed, making almost every shot. The first half ended with the Pirates leading 37-12. In the afternoon, Zhizhi remained unable to find a solution. Due to their smaller stature, their passing and interceptions were consistently outmaneuvered. Given the significant disparity in strength, the game proceeded smoothly without any surprises. The final result was 83-36.

Shanghai Chinese and Western, Japanese Four YMCA's Launch an Organization to Train Sports Referees; Established Yesterday, Two Main Leaders Were Selected to Proceed Separately; Initially Training Basketball Referees, Gradually Expanding to Other Items 250

The Shanghai YMCA, Western Overseas Chinese YMCA, Maritime YMCA, and Japanese Overseas Chinese YMCA, recognizing that Shanghai's sports industry is becoming increasingly prosperous, but the lack of sports referees with correct ideas and the insufficient number of personnel have become practical problems. Therefore, the organization of training sports referees was jointly initiated. The main leaders of the four associations consulted with each other, and a meeting was held yesterday to establish the organization, determine the outline, and put it into practice, which has a profound relationship with the advancement of Shanghai's sports industry. The meeting process is briefly described as follows:

General Assembly Declares the Purpose 251

Yesterday afternoon at 5:00 PM, the four groups that initiated this movement each sent representatives to attend the meeting. Mr. Topin, the chairman, first stated the purpose of the initiation. Then, according to his understanding, this type of organization does not conflict with the Chinese Referee Association, and the most important point is how to train and how to test, so as to become a legal sports referee. All experienced referees and those who hope to become a referee can participate. If they pass the training and examination, they will get a formal certificate stamped by the four groups.

Divided into Two Departments to Proceed 252

All representatives made good contributions to the progress of the matter. Finally, it was decided to divide into two major departments and select members to be responsible for the proceeding. The first department is the procedure department, which plans the training steps, and is chaired by Ling Xitao, Topin, Kaizhi and others. The second department is the examination department, which plans the examination methods, and is chaired by Qian Yiqin, Hall, Spia, and others. Generally, participants will first undergo two weeks of training, and then take the exam. Currently, the first step is to train basketball referees, gradually expanding to other items.

Page 14

Spring and Autumn

The Doctor and the Physician 253

— Yanqiao

Northerners call doctors "Daifu" (大夫), roughly borrowing the title from the Imperial Hospital. Those outside the hospital take pride in this title, and patients, hoping the doctor will put in more effort, also offer this respectful address, which over time has become the exclusive term. It's similar to how Southerners call doctors "Langzhong" (郎中).

I find that titles are the hardest things to change, and certainly can't be affected simply by issuing an order. I remember after the success of the Xinhai Revolution, Mr. Sun Yat-sen, in the Generalissimo's Office, ordered that everyone be addressed as "Mister," removing terms like "Your Excellency" and other honorifics. But how long did it take for "Your Excellency" to be revived? After the success of the Northern Expedition during the National Revolution, everyone was again to be addressed as "Comrade." However, this term was only fully applicable within the same organization; in other organizations, there was a risk of it not being honored. As for the general public, they remained completely "stuck in the old ways," just as things were under the rule of the Aisin Gioro.

However, Southerners say "Langzhong" orally, but write "Yisheng" (醫生, doctor) on paper, unlike Northerners, whose spoken and written language match, with newspapers also using "Daifu" in advertisements. When we Southerners see this, we easily think of the "Daifu" listed on obituaries, following "Chao Yi Feng Zhi" (朝議奉直), giving us a sense of "still seeing the old official rituals." Moreover, the character "Da" (大) is pronounced like "Dai" (代), which also easily evokes the image of storytellers using "Great King" (大王), giving it a bit of a rough air. However, the "Daifu" Lu from the Romance of the Three Kingdoms, who was terrified once by Zhuge Liang's arrow-borrowing with straw boats and again by Guan Yu's solo journey to the meeting, would find this "Taifu" (太夫) hard to be.

Materialists would say that whether it's "Daifu" or "Langzhong," the only thing that matters is the cure. That's why I saw that the school magazine of a certain university in Beiping still wrote "Please Mr. Daifu be the school doctor," combining "Daifu" and "school doctor" into one term, which I found very historically interesting.

Getting Better 254

— Qian Zuizhu

The phrase "Getting Better" is of course an auspicious expression. After a severe illness, the dangerous signs recede, and one is not doomed to be a dead man. This is one kind of "Getting Better."

Friendships sour, and there's talk of breaking ties. Through mediation, suspicions gradually dissipate. This is a second kind of "Getting Better."

A prodigal son turns back, studying and cultivating virtue. The family fortune declines, but he strives and works hard. Reviving what's declining and overcoming fatigue, gradually reaching a better state. This is a third kind of "Getting Better."

Examples like the above, in every aspect, are plentiful if you look for them using the principle of "a slap followed by a sweet."

China, a country with a great nation's demeanor and educated by ancient sages and worthies, values "not dwelling on past grievances." So, if someone receives a "spicy slap" from another, as long as they endure the momentary pain, they won't hold it against them; as the saying goes, "Great men don't remember the faults of small men." As for dwarfs, short people, and barbarians, there's even less point in teaching them, as it's not worth losing one's "gentlemanly demeanor." Don't say that children are ignorant and reckless, relying on love to offend superiors, which shouldn't be held against them; even if they intentionally offend, one should uphold the principle of compassion, pitying their ignorance and self-imposed guilt. Therefore, "offer the other cheek after being slapped on the left" is the only way to be worthy of being a great sage. Lou Shide's "letting saliva dry on his face" falls far short.

If people can think this way, not only will the slap not hurt, but it can also fully create a "disciple of sages," making one feel glorious and deeply grateful for the other person's act of completing one's virtue with a slap. The pain is worth mentioning, and there's certainly no hatred. One must know that the level of civilization of other countries is indeed somewhat lacking. They are straightforward, "good is good, bad is bad," and can't be as flexible and adaptable as the Chinese. Because of this, the "Getting Better" that can't be seen in other countries is especially common in China. This can be considered a source of pride for China, right?

Talking in One's Sleep 255

— Shen Yan

Once, I had a dream in which my good friend C suddenly committed suicide by jumping into the river due to a love affair. Fortunately, a sailor from a certain country was nearby and managed to save him from the river. This dream was very ordinary, but at that time, C was having a disagreement with his lover for some reason, and there was a possibility that my dream would become a reality. Determined to do something, the next day I went to his office to find him and told him the dream I had the night before, not only in great detail but also repeatedly using warning tones to sting him, implying that I was advising him to quickly bow his head and surrender to the lady. Whether he actually did so, I dare not say for sure, but C is still alive and well, and has not actually jumped into the Huangpu River, and his love affair is still ongoing. Only, every time I see him, I can't help but say to him, "Be careful not to jump into the Huangpu," and his reply is always, "Don't talk in your sleep."

Unfortunately, one day, he said his usual "Don't talk in your sleep" too loudly, which made me very uncomfortable, and we started with joking and ended up in a formal debate. But thanks to this debate, I developed a new understanding out of nowhere and used this new understanding to refute C until he was speechless. From then on, although I still teased him from time to time, "Be careful not to jump into the Huangpu," he no longer used the words "Don't talk in your sleep" as a reply.

I said, "Friend, don't think that there is a huge difference between dreams and reality, and don't take dreams too lightly. I'll just ask you two things: For example, getting rich is not an easy thing. Although you sincerely worship thrift and expanding income, and even don't hesitate to change all kinds of methods to try to get money, but facts tell us that ten people who want to get rich often fail together. It is true that getting rich in reality is not an easy thing. However, if you want to have a dream of getting rich tonight, can you guarantee that you will have this dream tonight? Of course not. Then the difficulty of dreaming is no less than that of reality. Secondly, I will ask you again what you did yesterday. Suppose you kissed a certain lady yesterday, but can you still keep this kiss today? Can you use any evidence to convince people that you kissed her yesterday? Isn't it just like dreaming, leaving some memorable impressions only in your own brain? People can also ridicule you for talking in your sleep, how can you guarantee what kind of result your kiss yesterday will produce in the future? Therefore, yesterday's facts are equal to dreams today. The facts that happened a minute or a second ago are also equal to dreams afterwards. Then what is the difference between recounting past facts or recounting dreams?"

New Nanny 256

— Yiqiu

She unbuttoned her clothes and put her nipple into the young master's mouth. She gently pinched her full breast with two fingers, and the little mouth could be heard "gulping" as it sucked her milk.

Her heart was filled with inexplicable sadness, and she said nothing, just staring blankly at a corner of the floor. "My milk cannot feed my own child: to be sucked by others: abandoned: my own flesh and blood: to raise someone else's child: they had children: they want someone else to feed them: I really want to feed my own child: I can't: away from my lovely hometown: to see terrible strange faces here:"

As she kept thinking like this, a gust of autumn wind seemed to carry the sound of a child crying from afar, "Ah: my darling! How are you now?" She couldn't bear the encirclement of this desolate image, and two teardrops fell miserably.

The young mistress walked past her and noticed the tear stains. She went back to her room, saw the "Old Huang Mama," and casually asked, "Why is the nanny crying?" Huang Mama said, "New nannies are always like this. Wasn't I like this when I first came out to help people? It's probably because they are new to the world and not worldly enough."

Sure enough, a year later, she gradually realized that this was a very natural thing, and she gradually realized that there were different "fates" among "people," so she lived a nanny life very contentedly.

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 257

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 20: Divination Brings Happiness, Old Man Smiles for Days; Endless Relief from Sorrow, Old Friends Live Across the Street

Madam Jiang said, "If you want to ask, but don't let me speak, I won't say it. I still need to go out." As she spoke, she took down a wooden box that was stacked on the kang, checked seven or eight pieces of clothing fabric inside, put them on the kang, wrapped them in an old bundle, and then moved the box back to its original place. When she climbed down from the kang, she saw Guizhi holding the bundle with her hands behind her back. Putting it behind her, she asked with a smile: "Where are you planning to take these fabrics?" Madam Jiang said, "I should give them to someone to make them, right?" Guizhi said, "You're so muddled, just hand them over to the tailor, and if they don't fit properly, it's not a big deal if the fabric is ruined, but if I don't like it, you'll say I'm nagging again." Madam Jiang said, "I was worried you wouldn't care. If you're willing to care, that's great, it'll save me from being worried and not meeting your expectations." Guizhi said, "I don't understand this. Why shouldn't I care about making my own clothes?" Her mother was afraid that she wouldn't care about the reason, and she really understood it, deliberately saying this to show that her heart was very calm, so she opened the bundle, took out only one piece of clothing fabric, wrapped it in a large silk handkerchief, and said to herself: "I'm also waiting to have clothes to wear, let Wang the Tailor make a rough piece first and try it out." Madam Jiang was also born as a maiden, knowing that maidens always have a kind of wanting to ask but not asking attitude towards their wedding clothes, so the mother can only vaguely act as a consultant, otherwise the maiden will become angry and ashamed. Because of this, Madam Jiang sat on the side, pretending nothing had happened. Guizhi also seemed to feel a little awkward about this matter. She stood in the house for a while, tidied up the things on the table, and saw that her mother didn't say anything, so she picked up the silk handkerchief package and walked out the door calmly. When she reached the door, she looked towards both ends of the street. Only then did she lower her head and walk step by step along the base of the wall. After walking halfway down the alley, she suddenly heard someone behind her calling out: "Miss, I haven't seen you for a long time, have you gone to the city to play again these few days?" (272)

Family Handicrafts 258

— Yan BOGuang

The Chinese family economy has always been solely borne by men, so there is an ancient saying, "It's hard for a hero to feed three mouths." We live in a modern society with an overpopulation. It is already very difficult to find a job, so where can you talk about thick or thin wages? If you are not willing to do it, someone will do it. So the Europeans and Americans once said this: It is not easy to find a thousand dogs in China immediately, but it is not difficult to gather a thousand people. It can be seen that the number of unemployed people is alarming! And the standard of living is so high. Women should do some small handicrafts in the family to earn some money to make up for the insufficient family expenses, so that your good man does not bear the burden alone. This is something that virtuous women will definitely be happy to hear. Today, I will introduce a few of them below. I hope you will work hard to produce and make your family economy more and more prosperous every day!

Snow Cream Making Method: Snow cream is the most popular in winter, and its sales are also very large. As long as you go to the material store to buy some bottles and go to the printing office to print some posters, the manufacturing method is very simple. Or make some bulk snow cream and put it in various cigarette paper stores for consignment sales, or wholesale it to barber shops. The resulting surplus profits are not small for the family economy. Its raw material blending method:

Stearin (you must buy the best, inferior products have a buttery smell.) Eight taels.

Sodium Carbonate, eight qian.

Filtered Water, twenty-five taels.

Glycerin, six taels.

Fragrance, eight qian or one tael. (Rose essence, jasmine essence, magnolia essence are all acceptable.)

The above are sold in Shanghai industrial raw material shops, or pharmacies. Its manufacturing method: First put the sodium carbonate into the filtered water and stir it with a stick to dissolve it. Use another enamel pot to crush the stearin and put it in the pot. Heat it over low heat. The heat should not be too high. It is best to prepare a Fahrenheit table and insert the mercury end to test it. About one hundred sixty or seventy degrees is the most suitable. After it is completely dissolved, pour the sodium carbonate water in six or seven times (about twenty-five taels of water dissolving sodium carbonate.) Each time you pour it in, it will cause an alkaline reaction. At first, it is dispersed due to being cold, and then it is alkalized by being heated again, until the alkaline liquid is finished (that is, sodium carbonate water.) At this time, the whole has already changed from a thin paste to a thick paste. At this time, stirring must be non-stop. After the water vapor is slightly evaporated, add glycerin and continue stirring. When the heat is slightly removed, add the essence. At this time, the golden body is cooled, and it changes from a thin body to a thick knot. At that time, the snow cream is complete, so divide it into bottles and put it for three or four days, and it will naturally reveal its brilliance and the fragrance is rich. Every winter, I always have to do it several times to prepare for the customers to buy separately. According to the above method, the snow cream must be very good.

Honey Cream Making Method: Honey cream is a blessing to the common people in winter. If you wipe it on, you can avoid chapped skin, and the capital is not large, and the method is easy. Like clam shell honey cream and tin box honey cream, the sales are very large. Its raw materials are:

White Vaseline, one tael.

Talcum Powder, six qian.

Candelilla Red Powder, appropriate amount. (Sold in paint stores.)

Rose Oil, appropriate amount.

Heat the Vaseline over low heat until it is melted. Add talcum powder, mix well, and add candelilla red powder to make a concubine color, or you can use all white without candelilla red powder. Remove from heat, mix in rose oil, and put it into the box while it is flowing. When it is cold, it will condense into a very good honey cream.

Silk Tea Silk Market Future Trends Are Increasingly Declining 281

(Silk factory industry is precarious) European and American silk sales have plummeted, and the silk factory industry in Jiangsu, Zhejiang and Shanghai has fallen into desperation. It is estimated that the silk stored in various ports has reached more than 10,000 dan, and the cocoons stored have exceeded 70,000 or 80,000 dan. Most of them are mortgaged to the financial sector, and the total silk and cocoon mortgages have reached 10 million. In the blink of an eye, the end of the year is approaching, and the silk factory industry is precarious due to the inability to repay and imminent bankruptcy.

(Double Palace silk sales are increasingly sluggish) Recently, the sales of Double Palace silk have become more and more sluggish. Only India has a slightly smaller appetite, and the British post office only exported 400 bales of Double Palace silk last week. The current sales are completely stagnant.

(Artificial silk customer sales turn clear) As the end of the year approaches, inland silk merchants' appetite for artificial silk has turned dull. Yesterday, only Hangzhou silk merchants entered 22 boxes of Feima, Yishu Sanqi, and other brands of current futures, and the price ranged from 175.75 yuan to 160 yuan net.

(Foreign silk dealers hold firm) The European and American markets are flooded with Japanese silk, and the current silk price in New York is difficult to rise. The price of French silk in Lyon is high and no one asks about it. The dispatches from Shanghai are still not turning around. Although Chinese silk merchants are eager to sell due to the accumulation of silk near the end of the year, the current selling price is not enough to cover the principal and interest of the mortgage, and they are willing to put the stored silk on hold and suspend business to wait for a turnaround next year. Therefore, the market atmosphere is holding firm and there is no news of current silk transactions. The future of the silk industry is becoming increasingly dangerous.

The Decline of Chinese Tea Sales in America 282

Chinese tea trade with America saw brisk sales and rising prices from August to October. However, recently, in the New York market, various types of green tea from the Ping Shui region of China, including Ma Zhu, Zhi Zhu, Zhen Mei, and Feng Mei teas, have experienced a sudden stagnation in sales. Merchants have accumulated a large stock of over 40,000 boxes. According to observations from tea merchants, the recent decline in American sales is due to the lifting of the alcohol ban in the United States, which has led to a surge in coffee sales. Furthermore, the massive import of Taiwanese and Japanese teas, sold at low prices, has contributed to the downturn.

The demand for genuine horsehair sleeve linings has increased significantly due to the popularity of lined overcoats, resulting in brisk sales. Prices have risen several times. Currently, domestic brands like "Dao Hua" are producing these linings day and night. Additionally, small-scale yarn and wool weaving factories in Shanghai, attracted by the potential profits, are also manufacturing similar products, leading to a sudden increase in supply and a slight dampening of the market. The price increases for imported goods have ceased. Yesterday, wholesale prices for imported genuine horsehair sleeve linings were uniformly one dollar and sixty-five cents (in foreign currency), domestic "Dao Hua" goods were one dollar and thirty-five cents, and products from miscellaneous small factories were priced at one dollar and twenty-five cents per yard.

Additionally, lock companies, coppersmiths, and other trades also have a need for it, making the market outlook very optimistic.
