Free Discussion

The Ancient City Meeting 285

— Cao Juren

"The Ancient City Meeting" is a well-known old opera featuring a black-faced character and a red-faced character arguing (please forgive an outsider for speaking like an outsider). I recently watched this play again at the Xianxia Society and suddenly thought of Mr. So-and-so's speech about restoring old virtues. I felt that this fixed-form morality, performed and interpreted by millions of people, should be at the forefront of any restoration.

The black-faced third brother had always admired and obeyed the red-faced second brother. However, on this occasion, he became highly suspicious, practically denying the red-faced brother's character. It was as if a prostitute who had already sold herself was shouting about chastity in the hands of her pimp, rendering it worthless. In the black-faced brother's eyes, the high position and generous salary offered by the Prime Minister's side had long captivated the red-faced brother's soul. The sworn brotherhood in the Peach Garden had been completely forgotten. How could someone who had gained the Prime Minister's favor still be willing to travel a thousand miles to return to Liu Bei? Therefore, refusing to open the gate was perfectly reasonable.

From our perspective as later generations, while the red-faced character is admirable, we can't help but laugh at his foolishness. If he had bowed down to the Prime Minister, he could have had wealth and women as he wished, enjoying great happiness. Returning to Liu Bei's side meant facing wind, frost, rain, and snow, a life of wandering and hardship. Rejecting "happiness" for "hardship" is something that at least the officials and scholars of today would never do. The various associations in Chinese lower society admire this red-faced hero who refused to serve the Prime Minister. If we want to find people of integrity, we should look among the lower classes. The ancients said that trustworthiness and righteousness were practiced by "gentlemen," but the term "gentleman" deserves careful consideration.

In the "Peach Blossom Fan" play, Ruan Da Yue instructs his servant to go to Jiming Dai to inquire about what the members of the Restoration Society thought of his critique of Yanzi Jian. When he heard them say, "A true talent, with an extraordinary pen, his writing is heavenly, an immortal exiled to the human world," his heart blossomed. But when he heard them say, "Why did he surrender to Cui and Wei, destroying himself?" he could only frown and sigh, "It's just this little bit of lack of talent; there's no need to talk about it anymore!" "There's no need to talk about it anymore" is something only officials and scholars would say. If the red-faced character said that, the black-faced character wouldn't buy it.

Even today, I would very much like to advocate for the old virtues, such as the ancient morality of "The Ancient City Meeting." However, who is qualified to advocate for this ancient morality is something to consider carefully. I fear nothing else but that the black-faced character will firmly refuse to open the gate, negating the red-faced character's integrity!

Conditions for Translating Famous Works 286

— Kanran

At a time when young people feel there are no books to read and lack spiritual nourishment, and when several large bookstores are focused on competing in the textbook market and unwilling to publish translated works, the Zhongshan Cultural and Educational Center's proposal to systematically translate Western classics is naturally very exciting.

Originally, systematically introducing Western classics requires significant capital. It is appropriate for the Zhongshan Cultural and Educational Center, with the help of the government and private individuals and sufficient funding, to undertake this major cultural endeavor. It is said that the Center plans to pay translators five yuan per thousand words and also allow them to collect royalties upon publication. With such conditions, I believe good translation results should be achieved.

However, systematically introducing world classics is not easy. Even with substantial financial resources, it must be handled properly. If done well, it will have a great and positive impact on our culture. Otherwise, it will not only waste money but also further tarnish the already chaotic translation field in the eyes of the world. Therefore, from a purely academic standpoint, I cannot help but offer some suggestions:

First, the selected classics must undergo careful scrutiny. Western classics are vast and boundless. Limited by manpower and financial resources, we must carefully select them after weighing their importance. I believe:

(1) Since it is a systematic introduction, we should select classics that have already received historical acclaim. Contemporary works should be selected sparingly.

(2) We should seek works from countries with deep European cultural roots. Newly emerging countries like Japan and the United States have few world-class scholars worthy of mention, so their works should be selected sparingly or not at all.

(3) Important works, even if they have already been translated, should be retranslated if the existing translation is not satisfactory.

(4) Truly valuable classics should be translated, even if it is known that few people will read them.

In short, the selection of classics requires gathering many specialized scholars with a deep understanding of Western culture to discuss them thoroughly. We do not know which classics the Center has already decided to translate, or which scholars selected the titles being translated. However, we have seen the list of review committee members in the newspapers. Unfortunately, while many of these members are highly respected figures, few have a deep understanding of Western culture. Some may not even understand any foreign languages. I believe the organizers need to add and remove members from this list.

Second, the translation of classics must strive for perfection. Translating classics should be a very serious matter. Since the Center has substantial financial resources, it should be able to obtain perfect translations. Failure to do so would not only mislead readers but also disrespect the Western sages who painstakingly wrote these works. To ensure perfect translations, I believe:

First, we must hire specialists with expertise in both Chinese and Western cultures to undertake the translations. Translating classics requires not only selecting people with extensive translation experience and excellent command of both Chinese and Western languages but also people who have specialized knowledge of the work they are translating. It would be inappropriate to have someone who studies engineering translate economic history, or to have someone who only knows how to translate novels translate AugComte's *Cours de Philosophie Positive*, a work of profound philosophy.

Second, classics must be translated from the original language. We know that no matter how good a translation is, it is always a significant step down from the original. This is especially true for philosophical works, where even the slightest error can lead to significant misinterpretations. In the past, China lacked translators, and many works from Germany and France were translated indirectly from English or Japanese, inevitably leading to errors from the initial translators. Now that there are many people proficient in German and French, there is no reason to continue using indirect translation methods.

I have many other personal opinions, but due to space limitations, I cannot present them all. Most importantly, I hope the Center will approach this translation of world classics with a determination to serve culture and sacrifice for scholarship, without any intention of profiting or pursuing other aims. Printing and distribution can be entrusted to bookstores, but the selection of classics must not be influenced by bookstores. Otherwise, there is a risk of being swayed by the desire for sales and catering to the market, neglecting truly valuable classics in favor of second- or third-rate Western works or recently published, ephemeral works from Japan or the United States for speculative gain. Let me reiterate: the success or failure of the Center's translation of world classics has a tremendous impact on the future of Chinese culture. Not only should the organizers take it seriously, but the entire writing and reading community in China should pay close attention to it.

Nalan Chengde's Poetic Theories (Continued) 287

— Chen Liang

II

Nalan Chengde's unique feature of his poetic theory is his anti-imitation stance. Like many poets, he advocates creativity, advocating that each era should have poetry adapted to that era. In his jottings, he used great effort to oppose the tendency to imitate, providing various proofs from a theoretical and phonological standpoint. In general, he says: "The study of ancient poetry is like an infant who cannot do without a wet nurse. Only after standing on one's own can poetry be formed, just as only after standing on one's own can one become an adult. Those in the Ming dynasty who studied Du Fu and the High Tang spent their entire lives being fed at the wet nurse’s breast."

The metaphor of "spending one’s days at the wet nurse's breast" is apt. In another passage, he poses the question, "Regulated verse is a recent form. Its opening, introduction, transition, and conclusion are similar to the style of the eight-legged essay, except without the introductory, supporting, and explanatory paragraphs. Ancient verse, however, (there seems to be something missing here, or perhaps it's a duplicated phrase) is like the essays of Ou and Su, endlessly changing. Those who write eight-legged essays mostly dare not presumptuously write ancient prose, but those who write regulated verse all attempt to write ancient verse. Is this permissible?" It is evident that these imitationists exhibit contradictions even within themselves and lack a unified understanding. Regarding phonology, Nalan Chengde says:

"The greatest harm to poetry today comes from writing rhyming verse. There was a slight tendency for this among Tang poets in the middle and late periods, and it became prevalent in the Song dynasty, hence the Yuan dynasty's compilation of the *Yunfu Qunyu* [a rhyming dictionary]. Today, poetry without rhyming verse is considered unusual! If one's poetry cannot rival that of one's predecessors, and one further binds one's own hands to face the enemy, that is an extreme miscalculation! I once said this to a friend, and he replied, 'People today are merely composing rhymes; who is composing poetry?' This statement is crucial and must be feared. If people do not abandon this illness, they will not produce good poetry." At the same time, in another passage, he also says, "When people compose poetry, they must base it on the *Three Hundred Poems*, but they do not follow its rhyming scheme. Is this not a reversal?" Just as in the general aspect, he points out the dead-end nature of imitationism as a form of "suicide," and in this phonological imitation, he similarly reveals its contradictory nature and advocates for breaking down this approach.

III

If he opposes imitationism, then what are Nalan Chengde's positive views on poetry? Based on the *Lushuiting Miscellaneous Records*, his views can be said to have two main targets: one is "expressing emotions," and the other is "expressing sentiments [寄託]." Regarding "expressing emotions," Nalan Chengde says:

"The *qu* style arose and lyrics declined, lyrics arose and poetry declined, Tang style arose and ancient poetry declined. The purpose of writing poetry is to express emotions. Living in the present era, recent forms are sufficient to express emotions. Scholars who admire the ancients lack those emotions and forcefully imitate the style to create ancient *yuefu* [ballads], which feels pointless."

This is similar to his statement that "poetry is the voice of the heart, a matter of temperament and emotions." In understanding, it is also similar to what Yu Quyuan later said: "Poetry that can enter the heart and spleen is a good work." His meaning is that poetry should not be imitation but should be the absolutely free expression of one's own feelings. Therefore, he says:

"People's feelings favor the new. Today, there is suddenly a fad for Song poetry. Those who wish to use scholarship to seek official positions are controlled by others, so they must follow others' steps. Poetry is for self-enjoyment; why should one follow others?"

"Poetry is for self-enjoyment; why should one follow others?" This insight is very incisive. "Expressing sentiments [寄託]" of course means "having content," having a definite theme. Connecting the two, Nalan Chengde's view is that poetry should have substantial new content and rich, genuine emotions. He says:

"The intention of Tang poets is not necessarily within the title, nor even within the poem itself, hence it is lofty and profound. Even when writing poems on objects, they must have sentiments to express and not create dead phrases. Today, when people discuss poetry, they are afraid that even a single word will stray from the title. This is good prose, not poetry."

This is just like his statement that "Tang poets have sentiments to express, so their use of allusion is skillful; later generations have no sentiments to express, so their use of allusion is rigid," advocating that poetry should have content and sentiments to express. In his jottings, he not only points this out in principle but also cites the poetry of Du Fu, Cao Tang, Han Wo, Liu Yuxi, Wu Yuanheng, and others as evidence.

Two Brothers (64) 288

— Translated by Mo Pasan (Maupassant), Li Weike

She had decorated this bedroom with all of a mother's love. The walls were covered with linen from Rouen, imitating ancient Normandy fabrics. A Louis XV bed, an armchair carved with irises and doves' beaks on the arms, filled the walls and furniture with a charming rustic flavor.

"Ah! It's beautiful," said Mrs. Lu, looking slightly serious as she entered the room.

"Do you like the house?" Zhe'an asked her.

"I like it very much."

"You know how happy I am to hear that."

They gazed at each other with affectionate eyes.

However, she felt slightly awkward and somewhat confused in this bedroom, which would become her marital chamber. She noticed upon entering that the bed was extremely large, definitely a bed for a married couple. Mrs. Luo Lan had chosen this bed, and she certainly expected and hoped that her son would soon realize his marriage plans. This thoughtfulness on the part of the mother pleased her greatly, as it was tantamount to saying that this family was waiting for her.

Later, when everyone returned to the living room, Zhe'an suddenly opened the door on the left, and everyone saw the circular dining room with three windows and Japanese lanterns. Mother and son had used all their ingenuity to decorate this room. With its bamboo furniture, porcelain dolls, colorful pottery, brocades, transparent curtains adorned with raindrop-like glass beads, fans attached to the walls to absorb the wallpaper, and all the porcelain, wooden, paper, ivory, mother-of-pearl, and bronze trinkets, the room had an affectation and pretense born of insensitivity, lack of taste, or the clumsy blindness of the artistically uneducated. However, it was the room everyone admired the most. Bi Er made a few less-than-complimentary remarks with a slightly bitter mockery, and his younger brother immediately felt displeased.

Fruit was piled on the table like pyramids, and desserts were piled high.

But no one was hungry at all; they just sipped on some fruit and tasted the desserts. After almost an hour, Mrs. Lu got up to say goodbye.

Luo Lan the Elder decided to take her to her doorstep and set off with her immediately. As for Mrs. Luo Lan, because the maid was not there, she had to look around the house to make sure her son didn't lack anything.

"Shall I come back to pick you up?" Luo Lan the Elder asked.

She hesitated for a moment, then replied:

"No, you go back to sleep. Bi Er will take me back."

After he left, she blew out the candle, put the desserts, candies, and various liqueurs in the cabinet, locked it, and handed the key to Zhe'an. Then she went into the bedroom, uncovered the quilt, checked if the water jug was full of ice water, and made sure the windows were closed.

Bi Er and Zhe'an stayed in the small living room. Zhe'an was still displeased because his older brother had criticized his taste, and Bi Er became increasingly angry as he watched his younger brother live in this house.

They both sat smoking without speaking. Bi Er suddenly stood up and said:

"That widow looked tired tonight. The excursion didn't make her look any better."

Zhe'an suddenly felt the sudden rage of a heartbroken weakling.

He was so angry he couldn't breathe. He stammered:

"I won't allow you to call Mrs. Lu a 'widow' when you speak of her again!"

Bi Er turned to him and said arrogantly:

"You seem to be giving me orders. Are you crazy?"

Talking Points

Scientific Inventions and Control 289

— Lizhai

Whenever we mention science, we inevitably think of the two figures of modern times who have contributed the most to human life: one is Edison, who invented the light bulb, telephone, and phonograph and was hailed as the "Conqueror of the World's Mysteries," who passed away two years ago, and the other is Marconi, who invented the radio and recently visited Shanghai.

Originally, the history of mankind is the history of two-legged animals struggling to conquer nature with reason and technology. Any great scientist or inventor is first and foremost a great teacher who uses extraordinary genius, painstaking thought, and difficult experiments to guide mankind to conquer nature, thereby earning universal adoration. The reason why Edison's death was mourned worldwide and why Marconi's visit to China was met with fervent and sincere welcome is because of this.

Modern science has reached the stage where sound, light, chemistry, and electricity are controlled with ease, but in the vast and endless universe, we humans do not know how far we are from completely conquering and controlling nature. Therefore, for the sake of a richer life and greater happiness for mankind, we still need many future scientists and inventors to create even greater and more brilliant chapters in the history of mankind. However, familiar with the weaknesses and sins of mankind, we must add here in extra-large letters: While we certainly need more scientists and countless future inventions, we especially need to transfer the control of all science from the hands of a few imperialists and wealthy magnates to the majority of mankind! This righteous and stern statement can be explained from the following points:

First, in the past painful history of the European War and the current mad preparations for a second world war, all imperialists are desperately concentrating the application of science on the path of human massacre. As a result, science, which was originally intended to increase human happiness, has become a terrible weapon for a few ambitious people to abuse the human race. For example, the rapid development of bacteriology was originally the greatest progress in medicine, but in the hands of imperialists, various bacteria that are most likely to harm life have become disguised shells. In addition, the use of radio to spy on other countries' military and political secrets in order to prepare for war, the use of electricity to torture political prisoners, and the use of chemistry to manufacture poisonous gas are all caused by the control of politics and science by a few ambitious people. Therefore, to make science the science of humanity and not a "weapon of murder," we must seize control of science from the hands of a few international individuals and return it to the majority of mankind!

Second, precisely because imperialism used science to massacre more than eight million soldiers, create tens of millions of widows and orphans, and destroy countless people's wealth in the European War, many "metaphysical ghosts" and idealists seized the opportunity to pontificate after the war, saying that "science caused the evils of the European War," advocating that mankind should "talk less about science" and pay more attention to "spiritual life." This kind of sermon, on the one hand, is to exonerate the few people who control science from the responsibility of the war, and on the other hand, it is to slander science and scientists with "false accusations." Therefore, to truly benefit mankind, politically-minded scientists would never want the scientific contributions they have wrung their brains and spent their blood on to continue to be controlled and used by a few as weapons to create human tragedies or evils. Because it is a matter of gnashing teeth for every scientist that a few people steal the "key to human happiness" from the scientist's laboratory and use it as a "weapon of evil."

Third, as far as our China is concerned, the vast majority of wealthy gentry, masters, and madams do not know how to correctly

Page 18

utilize science. People use the radio to broadcast noble music, send important news, and convey academic ideas in lectures, while Chinese madams and gentlemen install broadcasting machines to "fulfill vows" by broadcasting the Diamond Sutra or the Heart Sutra, or install radios to "enjoy" "crying marvelous...Duye"! Therefore, if the control is not in the right hands, things related to science, even in China, are not necessarily of much benefit to ordinary people!

Finally, I would like to extend my full respect to Mr. Marconi, the inventor of the radio, who recently visited China. At the same time, to sincerely respect science, I also extend the curse of "when will you perish" to the few who control science and use it to create evil!

"One-Legged" Bottom Show 290

— Of

The day before yesterday, Shanghai newspapers carried a Reuter's telegram from Guangzhou with a decorative border: "A soldier who lost a leg in the Shanghai war bought a single shoe from a shoe store. The owner refused, leading to a beating. He was then taken to court and sentenced: Shoes must be bought in pairs. If only one shoe is bought, the store owner is right to refuse."

Among the Chinese soldiers who have fought in civil wars for more than twenty years, the number of crippled and amputated wounded is, of course, countless. Wounded soldiers causing trouble in various places has also become a common and uncontrollable phenomenon. Precisely because there are so many of them that they cannot be counted, precisely because it is universally uncontrollable, people have probably become accustomed to it and have not paid serious attention to it. The one-legged soldier in the Reuter's telegram was once an "anti-Japanese hero" who fought fiercely against the Japanese "Imperial Army" in Shanghai. In terms of merit, he should not be inferior to the "Cai Tingkai" and others. The country and the people should treat this disabled brother who fought in the "national war" with special consideration and provide him with considerable convenience and preferential treatment in his life. But unfortunately, the country is too chaotic, and no one pays attention to the wounded soldiers. As a result, the humorous news of this one-legged disabled soldier buying a single shoe from a shoe store became known throughout the country through the Reuter's telegram.

This is a small matter. Probably leisurely people will not regard this news as some kind of humorous relaxing material, like gossiping about love affairs with relish, because in the eyes of those people, this matter is extremely absurd—can shoes sold in pairs be split up and bought one by one? In such a society, the judge's verdict is truly fair and decisive!

However, "fair and decisive" has so easily concealed this simple, ordinary, but actually very complex and serious social problem!

China has civil wars every year, China's army increases every year, the villages are sparsely populated, the fields are all barren, and the strong young men are subjected to the oppression of life and run to the front lines of the civil war. How cruel war is! The people's livelihood drives this countless hungry group under the artillery fire, ruthlessly destroying—death and injury!

China's army is larger than any other country in the world, but the lives of Chinese soldiers are more miserable than those of soldiers in any other country in the world. Other countries' armies do not fight civil wars, other countries' armies have a prosperous life, common entertainment, perfect training, and barracks. The Chinese army has to drag its guns and go to the front line to fight desperately, without salary, without entertainment, without training, without barracks, without anything, but they have to drag their guns and fight desperately!

Today, the psychology of the Chinese people is that everyone is afraid and disgusted when they see soldiers. This is because Chinese soldiers have ideas as soon as they see the common people, they are hungry and want to grab food from the people, they have no entertainment and want to find village women for pleasure, they sleep in the wilderness and want to forcibly occupy civilian houses. All of this is the unavoidable suffering of Chinese soldiers and the misfortune of the common people. When we look at these sufferings and misfortunes, who can we blame? Where should reason and conscience be found?

Central Government Stops Abetting Manchurian Autonomy

On the battlefields of civil war, the soldiers who are tragically injured, what merit do they have to the country and the people? But the wounded soldiers in the past have relied on their hard work and high merits to be arrogant and invincible. They are not arrogant to military officers, but only vent their depressed anger on the common people, and the common people suffer misfortune. Who can be blamed for this? If you ask him for whom he was injured, he will be menacing, but he does not know for whom or for what he was injured.

It is said that the one-legged soldier's leg in the Reuter's telegram was lost in the "national war" in Shanghai. This leg of his was for the honor of the country and the nation, and the people should not feel disgusted, right? But "one-legged only needs one shoe," "shoes must be bought in pairs," who can say who is right and who is wrong in this conflict of interests?

Only the judge is fair and decisive: "Shoes must be bought in pairs. If only one shoe is bought, the store owner is right to refuse."

Thus, this one-legged soldier will never be able to buy shoes in this world for the rest of his life! Is this a tribulation he should have in his fate?

From this small matter, we can see how bad our country has become! The country is unfortunate, everything is impossible, reason, conscience, law::: what meaning do we see these things play in the world? Alas, what meaning do they play?:::

Rat Infestation 291

— Wen Bing

My apartment has always had rats, but recently they have become more and more numerous, leading to a terrible rat infestation.

It was one day, I was still sleeping greedily, the sound of washing chamber pots in the alley had long been silent, the time was certainly after nine o'clock, suddenly I was awakened by the sound of "sa sa sa", I opened my drowsy eyes and found that the shirt hanging on the east corner was moving. Speaking of this shirt, although it has a very deep relationship with me—it is my close-fitting clothes, and the material is so good, it is silk. But as soon as the weather turned cooler, I seemed to dislike it, letting it hang alone in the east corner, too lazy to tidy it up, and too lazy to take it to wash. However, this thing is not bad, except that the substance itself is green, and it has accumulated a lot of grease from my body, which is exactly what cunning rats love most. When I got out of bed to look, I found that the front, back, and cuffs were gnawed into countless holes. I also let it hang as it was, not wanting to mend it or take it to wash.

This matter was known to Wu Jun, who lived in the same room, and he was very angry. He picked up a fly swatter and searched in all directions of the corner. At this time, I sat back on the bed, too lazy to wipe my face, just staring at Wu Jun in a daze, maybe Wu Jun was blaming me for not helping him.

Of course, I also hated that the rats gnawed my clothes. However, I felt that this was because the room was too messy. If you want to avoid rat infestation, you must first tidy up the room and throw away all the bad things. Why are there no rats in Mrs. Mei's house? There are none in Brother Yi's house either. It turns out that their apartments are very clean and tidy, and all the bad things are piled up separately. I also wanted to do this. However, I was too昏庸and lazy, just talking about it. Although I tried my best to throw away the bad things, there were still so many, and the room was still messy.

Recently, there have been more and more rats. They have no scruples and come out during the day, somersaulting by my feet. Humph, this really makes me angry and amused, but I am too lazy to care, and when they slip away a little, I just let it go.

I don't know why, but I thought of the large white cat raised by the second landlord, so I went to visit the second landlord and told him about my rat infestation in detail. He said that rats are the most hateful, and I have a large white cat here, you can catch it and use it. So I caught the white cat, I respected it as my only savior. Sure enough, the first night was relatively quiet, and the rats did not make such a mess of overturning boxes and cabinets. But after a long time, it returned to its previous state. It turned out that although the white cat was large, it was useless. It only knew how to eat, only knew how to scream, and even defecated everywhere. The rats knew that the white cat was so useless, so they unscrupulously made trouble again. Sometimes they even teased the white cat together. The white cat probably knew that it was originally useless, so it secretly ran back. Wu Jun originally did not agree to catch the white cat, knowing that it was useless. If you want to get rid of the rat infestation, you can only work hard to fight and catch it yourself, which is a simple way.

After the white cat left, the rats became even more violent. I was too lazy, and after a long time, I became calm about it. The shirt hanging in the east corner has been gnawed so badly, just let it be, I don't want it anymore. Yesterday, I looked at a cotton robe hanging not far to the left, and there were also traces of rat gnawing, but I was still too lazy to tidy it up.

Wu Jun saw that I was so lazy and useless, and he was not interested in fighting anymore. He has not said anything for a long time. This morning, two friends came to visit, and they felt very sorry for me when they saw my rat-damaged items. They said they would think of a way for me, but there would be a reward, or the cotton robe would be given to them, or many photos hanging in front of the bed would be chosen by them, or some better and more valuable things in the suitcase would be given to them.

Saying a Few Fair Words for Women 293

— Shu

The Shen Bao on the 15th carried a statement by Mr. Shi Ying, a member of the Central Committee: "Women spend as much as more than 1.4 million yuan on cosmetics, perfumes, etc." This number is truly impressive! It is enough to show the extent of the total spending power of women. Even this small decoration among the thousands of decorations has been counted to be so alarming. If other more valuable items are added, it will be more than several million yuan?

Loving beauty is a very common mentality; especially for women, competing for beauty and vying for splendor, greatly showing off their style. But this phenomenon is ultimately artificial "affected creation." The ugly often overuse artificial means to make up for congenital defects, resulting in "overdoing it and spoiling it," making them look even uglier; if they are "naturally beautiful," then there is no need for such a thing, simply tidy up their clothes and keep them clean, the more simple the more natural and beautiful. Although it may not be like the famous French novelist, Colette, who would be "infatuated for several days" at first sight, it can at least save a lot of money. If one person can do this, and expand and universalize it, it may not be useless to the country and society. However, in this new era where everything is considered outdated unless it is fashionable, despite saying this, there is no impact at all. Who has the right to interfere or restrict it? They have money, the money is their own, and spending their own money is their duty, which can be said to be freedom. The word "also" in Mr. Shi Ying's statement seems to imply a little regret, but it can only be a regret. Moreover, other types of decorations besides swallowing grease cannot push the responsibility of consumption entirely on women. A group of modern men are also busy with consumption and busy with decoration, in order to meet the conditions they consider beautiful. Since women's hair has become fashionable with fluffy curls, things like hair oil have become exclusive consumer goods for men. Men and women are naturally matching animals, women want to please men, so they desperately work on their bodies and faces; and men want to take advantage of it, in order to win the other's attention, a smile, to the point of::::, naturally they also exhaust their ability to do what they can, and try their best to show off. "Since I flatter your beauty, you also please my face." Thus, they "love each other," "fly wing to wing," hug and kiss sweetly, live together and fly together, leisurely and carefree, and get what they want!" However, the point should be said back: consumption is shared by both sexes, and cannot be solely blamed on one aspect, but there is only a difference in the amount. For example: if the value of decorations reaches four million yuan, then a quarter of the consumption will undoubtedly be borne by modern men; women will certainly bear a heavier burden, let's say three quarters.

Amateur Mailbox 294

What should a son do?

Editor:

I am an apprentice. My parents have been married for more than ten years. Their relationship was originally very good, but in recent years my father married a woman outside, so he is indifferent to my mother. My father always gives most of the money he earns to this woman, while he gives nothing to my mother. This makes my mother cry day and night, and she is depressed and unhappy. My mother is an old-fashioned woman, not comparable to modern women, so she tries her best to endure and never mentions divorce. I feel that if this continues, my mother will either commit suicide or die of anger. Therefore, I hope that you will instruct my mother and son on the only way out as soon as possible, or a way to make my father realize his mistake. I am anxiously waiting for your reply. Respectfully,

Li Haoran

X X X

Editor's Note: According to the law, even if you are unwilling to file a "bigamy" lawsuit against Li Jun's father, you can also file a lawsuit against this woman for "obstructing the family"; this is a radical solution. However, after winning the lawsuit, it is hard to say whether Li Jun's father will not resent her even more because of this and restore the old feelings. This is when the law is exhausted!

If the material aspect can be barely maintained, then we advocate letting Li Jun's father go. Let him be free, and maybe he will have a day of self-awareness in the future. In addition, Li Jun should work hard to make progress, so that your mother can have considerable comfort in spirit and feel that there is still hope for the future. When a person has hope, "suicide" and "dying of anger" will naturally not be a problem.

Novel

Shanghai (23) 295

— Zhang Lao San

Uncle Thirty-Four's House

Talking to capitalists is not much different from meeting important people. It is not that I am dissatisfied with my uncle Xu Bingnan, I should "know the difficulty and retreat" and "know when to stop." Three years of hard life have made me understand everything. My uncle has clearly told you that there are not many days left this year, you have to wait for the opportunity to come next year. Originally, the opportunity flew in from the window, don't let it escape from the door. There are opportunities everywhere in life, what is the hurry at the end of this year when there are not many days left? Besides, I am still young, and there will be many, many more years to come!

That unexpected business and my cousin's encouragement are still a beautiful dream for me.

"Uncle, I'll come again another day." I stood up.

My uncle squinted his eyes and nodded, two thick white smokes spewing out from his nostrils, indicating that he was very satisfied with the handling of this matter.

"How can a nephew not eat at his aunt's house?" Second Aunt jumped up from the opium couch and raised her arm to look at her watch. "It's time for lunch, Eldest Miss, tell the kitchen to serve the food upstairs."

Hui-jie ignored her.

"Aunt, I'll come back to bother you another day. When I went out, my friends didn't know, I'm afraid they're waiting for me." I didn't wait for her to reply. "Uncle, I'm leaving. If there's anything, you can ask Hui-jie to write a letter to notify you."

"I know!" When Hui-jie pushed me out of the iron bed frame filled with opium smoke, that unique voice still came out from inside. "What's the point of being polite?"

Walking down the stairs, I walked out the door as if agreeing. The doorman's smiling face appeared from the doorway, bowing and saying:

"Miss, do you want a car?"

Hui-jie shook her head and sent me straight to the door. She didn't seem to have any intention of going back in. I hurriedly stopped her and said, "You don't have to see me off."

"I'm also going to the club to see Min-jie." She stared at the tips of her toes moving forward, as if thinking about something incredible.

I was embarrassed to stop her too much, and walked slowly side by side with her on the cinder road towards the tram stop in Xujiahui.

Thirty-Five A Warm Smile

I came and went on this cinder road three times under three different circumstances. The first time, I broke up with Min-jie and returned disappointed from the grand event of the sermon meeting, holding huge hopes. When I came out of the side door of the Fangwai Villa, I was like a lost dog, holding my own heavy steps. The second time, because of the misunderstanding of the love triangle, I secretly came to confess everything to my cousin on a clear morning in mid-May, but a half-day stay brought me two months of serious illness. Today, I revisit this cinder road full of scars, walking silently side by side with Hui-jie, recalling when she didn't recognize me and laughed and talked to her companions, I couldn't help but feel sentimental. No matter what, Hui-jie had an unstoppable emotion for me. Her recent everything towards me has been proven by facts. She wanted to snatch me from Min-jie's hands. I stepped on my own cluster of black shadows, and the sound of the cinder being crushed was like the blood in my heart boiling. I was surrounded in the arms of two different women, leaving the Zhengyi Society and attaching myself to my uncle. No matter whether his plan becomes a reality in a month, it makes no difference to me. However, I don't have any deep-seated hatred for Hui-jie. She accepted my advice and jumped out of the hell of urban girls for me, because she loves me; but I escaped from my hometown oppressed by evil forces, I have great hopes, now is not the time for us to fall in love.

I glanced at Hui-jie, her walking seemed to be pulled by something, and she also seemed to be counting her own steps. This short cinder road seems to be particularly long today. I mustered up the courage several times to say a few words that have been hidden in my heart for a long time to Hui-jie, but when they rushed to my throat, I couldn't say them. As we walked, the shadows on the ground gradually shortened, until they were completely trampled under our four legs. The sun has climbed to noon. Passing the small restaurant where I had a hearty meal, several rickshaws were parked in front of the door. The rickshaw pullers were gobbling down large bowls of rice. It seemed that they would never be bothered by anything, and after putting down their rice bowls, they dragged their empty cars to do their only job.

We stopped at the tram stop, and there was no tram coming from afar. When walking, we can barely maintain silent loneliness, but now we are standing next to the tram stop, and there are only two of us, so I was forced to say a word.

"Hui-jie, have you eaten?" I looked at the group of rickshaw pullers.

"Are you hungry?"

"I remembered eating a meal in this restaurant and being sick for two months." I shook my head and said:

"Why talk about the past? I'm not suffering from two months of illness?"

The tone of voice was so annoyed, finally I laughed myself, a sincere and warm smile.

Greta Garbo and John Gilbert Reunite on the Screen 296

— Zhao Yinian

"At any stage of my life, I have never been as happy as I am now. This is a new beginning, a new future; everything in the past is like a dirty mirror, wiped clean.

"For the first time in five years, I feel like I'm playing a role that I can play. This is a huge opportunity. I owe this joy and gratitude to Miss Garbo, but I have no hope of repaying it.

"I have had a very difficult time in my life. I am very surprised at how I fell from the heaven of lofty honor to the abyss where no one cares. But now, as quickly as before, and as surprisingly, I am on the road to revival. What a strange experience!

"It is a great honor to work with Miss Garbo on the screen again. She is a great artist, a great woman. It is no secret that it is because of her ability that I can play this role. She believes in my misfortune and wants to correct people's mistakes about me. My only hope and desire is how should I do it, so that I can live up to her confidence in me." John Gilbert said this.

"This is Colossal" is a phrase that John Gilbert used to say.

Ignoring all opposition and gossip, Garbo worked hard to convince the MGM authorities to sign a contract with John to be the male lead in her new film.

They met - John was nervous and confused in this unexpected good news. As for Garbo, who knows what she felt and what she thought?

After all, our brave John opened his mouth first. "Great!" he said happily. In Garbo's heart, this phrase that John used to say often suddenly invaded. Eight years ago, when they started filming "Flesh and the Devil," this Colossal English word was the first word that John taught our shy and clumsy Swedish girl."

From the time John married Jna Claira until he signed this contract, they had not met or spoken. During these years, they worked in the same studio. Garbo rose steadily, stepping on the ladder of happiness; John, on the other hand, fell until he could barely see any light.

John's reputation declined day by day. Only because of the contract, MGM had to pay him his salary as before. As soon as the contract expired, he was immediately fired. In these long years of misfortune, he had almost no achievements. It was extremely difficult for him to come to the studio. When he met old friends on the road, he hid like a snake, hoping that they would not see him. He considered himself a failure in a permanently unrecoverable position, and his name would never shine in the electric light again.

John, who was kicked out of MGM, went to Fox Company to try his luck. (Many years ago, he had filmed "The Count of Monte Cristo" at Fox.) He also tried to be a director. But they all failed.

John's former fame was extinguished like a fire. What a huge shame! This black-faced, big-eyed hero once intoxicated the hearts of many young girls. Young girls took their lovers to the cinema to see John, hoping that they would learn from John. But why was he so unfortunate?

But, miss, please don't be discouraged. A woman named Garbo has brought John back to you. She was his sweetheart once. She is a great woman. She brought back his bright future to him. His failure caused her more pain and more thoroughly in her heart than he did himself. Although this is not specific pain.

"Queen Christina" is the film she starred in with John. The part of the script about John was rewritten by her, especially suitable for John's personality. She believes that this film can restore his lost glory. (Omitted below)

Film Review

Review of "Pigeon Loft Romance" 297

— Ling He

(RatterRomancee)

丨Produced by RKO, Premiered in Shanghai丨

A humorous film.

However, we find that the author has indeed portrayed the landlord very well. Renting out an extremely simple rooftop room to both a man and a woman simultaneously, while ensuring both tenants are satisfied; stingy, cunning, and meticulously calculating even the smallest amounts of money – a complete sketch of a petty urbanite. The unique demeanor of a small merchant is vividly and realistically depicted by the author, making him very lively and lovable.

People like this are indeed very familiar to urban dwellers, and therefore, such a character can easily evoke genuine empathy in us.

Similarly, the author's depiction of the lives of the two tenants, a man and a woman, who belong to the lower middle class, is also very realistic. The young woman, due to financial constraints, had to move from a large room to the attic, and share it with another man, taking shifts. The man, when caught in heavy rain, had no clothes to change into and had to wait fifteen minutes at the laundry entrance, soaked in the rain. :: Such struggles of lower middle-class people for survival, and their various lifestyles, are portrayed in a way that is close to reality.

But what is the author's attitude towards these things? Instead of portraying them directly, he beautifies their lives with a humorous approach. Of course, we are not against the use of comedy, but for certain themes, the comedic form reduces the seriousness of the drama. If someone were to ask, haven't Charlie Chaplin's portrayals of lower middle-class life also been in the form of comedy? True. However, the author of this film is far inferior to Charlie Chaplin.

In order to create humor and gags, a very far-fetched story is constructed. A man and a woman living in the same house, how can they not know each other for a long time? This kind of coincidence is not believable. As for writing about them being in love with each other, while also showing them being pursued by another person of the opposite sex, it clearly doesn't give people a good impression and only serves the interest of the story itself.

Here, it seems to approach the issue of housing. Regardless of whether the author intentionally lightens a serious issue, one can recognize that American films are beginning to pay attention to social problems in the choice of subject matter. This is a previously rare situation.

Hollywood's Newly Discovered Companionate Divorce 298

— Fu

Hollywood is truly a place where anything can happen, and the styles of marriage and divorce are especially numerous. We may have heard of it, but many people must still not understand what is called a Companionate Marriage. But now, a new type of Companionate Divorce has been added. What is a Companionate Marriage? Simply put, it means that after marriage, each person continues their original life. Either they continue to live separately, or they live together, and everyone does not interfere with each other's freedom. In short, the life between a couple is like the relationship between two friends. Speaking of Companionate Divorce, simply put, it means that a married couple is now separated, but not divorced. Not only are they not divorced, but they can still visit each other or have a one or two-day gathering, after making an appointment. Why practice this kind of Companionate Divorce? First, it may be because each spouse has their own career, and living together can be distracting. Household chores, in particular, can easily deprive women of their freedom, so they agree to live separately. Second, it may be that the couple has disagreements, but their feelings have not completely broken down, so they come up with this method as an excellent compromise.

Who invented this Companionate Divorce? It turns out that it was invented by Hollywood star Gloria Stuart and her husband Gordon Newell. Newell is an artist specializing in sculpture. The couple's feelings have not broken down, but because each person has their own career, they feel that living together is uneconomical in terms of time and energy, so they agreed to live separately. Before they separated, a reporter interviewed them. They even talked to the reporter about the meaning of Companionate Divorce. Newell's main idea was that the meaning of their separation was not in the words "separation," but in the words "division of labor," which is simply separating to work. Stuart said: "My job is to make films. I should spend all my time in the studio. Therefore, I can no longer take care of Gordon's affairs. And living together, everyone's time and work are hindered, so we can't help but think of a win-win solution. That is the "Companionate Divorce" we want to implement."

Curing One Disease Cures All Diseases 299

— Fu

Clark Gable Benefits from Misfortune

Clark Gable had a serious illness this autumn, and almost passed away. Now he has gradually recovered. Not only has his illness improved, but the doctor says he can also be healthy into old age. What's the reason? Originally, Clark Gable had two dangerous ailments. One was the decay of the tonsils in his throat, and the other was severe appendicitis. Since joining Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer, he has been extremely busy with work, so although his health was getting worse, he never had time to have them treated due to the pressure of work. This time is different. He had a serious illness and almost died. Therefore, he listened to the doctor's orders and decided to solve these two ailments fundamentally. So, after his serious illness slightly improved, he first had his throat operated on to treat the inflammation of his tonsils. After his throat slightly improved, he then had his abdomen opened. This was originally a last-ditch effort, but unexpectedly, Clark Gable was able to achieve good results, and since his two fatal ailments have been removed, the doctor said that he can live a long life.

Submission Guidelines for Shenbao Film Special 300

This publication is a film journal that assists in cultural promotion and artistic expression. We welcome external submissions and offer generous compensation upon publication.

Once text is published and compensated, the copyright belongs to Shenbao.

The language of this publication is primarily modern vernacular Chinese and must use modern punctuation.

If the submission is a translation, the original work should be attached. If English is mixed in, it should be avoided where possible.

Due to limited space, the text should be as concise as possible. Each submission should be around 500 words.

Unless previously stated and accompanied by a return envelope and postage, we are not responsible for preserving or returning text, photos, etc.

Submissions sent to multiple publications, plagiarized text, or direct transcriptions of instructions will not be compensated upon discovery.

Each submission must be stamped with a seal; otherwise, it will be rejected for compensation.

Do not write on both sides of the paper, write horizontally, or use a pencil.

Film Novel Little Women (15) 301

— Su Yin

Bael listened to Qiao quietly, and he suddenly understood the meaning of Laurie and Amy's marriage. He shyly took Qiao's hand, and he said, "Please wait a moment. I have something to say to you." He was very timid at first, but he finally stuttered and continued, "I am too bold, I don't have the courage to think, but I dare" hope that you can leave some space in your heart for a person who is not very lucky::: Oh, I know I shouldn't be so presumptuous to ask you this question at this time, your heart is too full of happiness now | but I can come back another day, if you let me come back to see you. I am now in Boston, and have found a position, so丨" He stopped here, he looked at Qiao's face very sincerely. For a while, everyone stood silently facing each other, each with their own secret thoughts. Their faces. Very slowly, a new kind of joy gradually emerged. Then Qiao grabbed Bael's arm and pulled him inside. She introduced him to everyone with great pride. She told many things about their time in New York, but the new secret about the two of them | that was too sweet and too precious, and it was not yet time to reveal it | Finally, she said, "He brought a book, my book has now been published.

Then everyone clamored around, congratulating her and scrambling to see the new book. They warmly welcomed Professor Bael, thanking him for all the kindness he showed to Qiao. Bael also talked to them very generously, calling out each person's name, which obviously surprised everyone. So Qiao told them, "He knows you all, because your names are all in my book, so he knows them." Bael said, "But you don't have to worry, Qiao wrote with a loving pen, which can make the readers laugh and rejoice with you." After he finished speaking, he looked around as if looking for something he had been away from for a long time. He suddenly saw the piano, and he said in a low voice, "Oh, this is the piano."

"Bael, please sit down and play," Qiao said. So Bael sat down without hesitation, and his hand lightly touched the piano keys, and immediately as if turning stone into gold, the piano emitted a melodious tone. Everyone listened quietly, and deep emotions appeared on everyone's faces. Then Bael began to sing again. Mr. Laurence leaned back in his chair, his eyes closed. John Brooke secretly held Meg's hand, and Meg responded with a sweet smile. The old aunt's face, which was full of frost, seemed to have melted. Laurie and Amy stood next to the piano, Laurie's hand around Amy's slender waist. What about Qiao? Looking at Bael's dilapidated appearance, she seemed to have already fallen deeply in love. She asked her mother in a low voice, "Do you think he is good? Her mother wiped away her happy tears, nodded to indicate her permission, and thought that Qiao's romance, which she had always thought would not blossom, was now flourishing there. (The End)
